text-align: center;">\n         0.7%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">\n         Source: 1910\xe2\x80\x932010\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n          <a href="#cite_note-77">\n           [77]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <br/>\n         2015 Estimate\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population">\n        Population\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       From just over 45,000 residents in 1800, Ohio\'s population grew at rates of over 10% per decade (except for the 1940 census) until the\n       <a href="/wiki/1970_United_States_Census" title="1970 United States Census">\n        1970 census\n       </a>\n       , which recorded just over 10.65 million Ohioans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Growth then slowed for the next four decades.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       estimates that the population of Ohio was 11,613,423 on July 1, 2015, a 0.67% increase since the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 United States Census\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio\'s population growth lags that of the entire United States, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_race" title="Caucasian race">\n        Caucasians\n       </a>\n       are found in a greater density than the United States average. As of 2000\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Ohio\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">\n        center of population\n       </a>\n       is located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Morrow_County,_Ohio" title="Morrow County, Ohio">\n        Morrow County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POPCENTER_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-POPCENTER-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">\n        county seat\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gilead,_Ohio" title="Mount Gilead, Ohio">\n        Mount Gilead\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POPCEN_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-POPCEN-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is approximately 6,346 feet (1,934\xc2\xa0m) south and west of Ohio\'s population center in 1990.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POPCENTER_81-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-POPCENTER-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population_Growth_Ohio.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="516" data-file-width="859" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Population_Growth_Ohio.png/220px-Population_Growth_Ohio.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Population_Growth_Ohio.png/330px-Population_Growth_Ohio.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Population_Growth_Ohio.png/440px-Population_Growth_Ohio.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population_Growth_Ohio.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Graph of Ohio\'s population growth from 1800 to 2000.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As of 2011, 27.6% of Ohio\'s children under the age of 1 belonged to minority groups.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       6.2% of Ohio\'s population is under 5 years of age, 23.7 percent under 18 years of age, and 14.1 percent were 65 or older. Females made up approximately 51.2 percent of the population.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_data">\n        Birth data\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Note: Births in table don\'t add up, because Hispanics are counted both by their ethnicity and by their race, giving a higher overall number.\n       </i>\n      </p>\n      <table   139,264\n         </b>\n         (100%)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">\n        Ancestry\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       According to the 2010\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" title="United States Census">\n        United States Census\n       </a>\n       , the racial composition of Ohio was the following:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">\n         White American\n        </a>\n        : 82.7% (\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">\n         Non-Hispanic Whites\n        </a>\n        : 81.1%)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_American" title="Black American">\n         Black or African American\n        </a>\n        : 12.2%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n         Native American\n        </a>\n        : 0.2%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">\n         Asian\n        </a>\n        : 1.7%\n        <small>\n         (0.6% Indian, 0.4% Chinese, 0.1% Filipino, 0.1% Korean, 0.1% Vietnamese, 0.1% Japanese)\n        </small>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">\n         Pacific Islander\n        </a>\n        : 0.03%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n         Two or more races\n        </a>\n        : 2.1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Some other race: 1.1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_or_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic or Latino Americans">\n         Hispanic or Latinos\n        </a>\n        (of any race) make up 3.1%\n        <small>\n         (1.5% Mexican, 0.8% Puerto Rican, 0.1% Guatemalan, 0.1% Cuban)\n        </small>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">\n       <caption>\n   \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census"     <td>\n         1.1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n          Two or more races\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1.4%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2.1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       In 2010, there were 469,700 foreign-born residents in Ohio, corresponding to 4.1% of the total population. Of these, 229,049 (2.0%) were naturalized\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Citizenship" title="US Citizenship">\n        US citizens\n       </a>\n       and 240,699 (2.1%) were not.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The largest groups were:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       (54,166),\n       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n        India\n       </a>\n       (50,256),\n       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">\n        China\n       </a>\n       (34,901),\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       (19,219),\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       (16,410),\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">\n        United Kingdom\n       </a>\n       (15,917),\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       (14,223),\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russia\n       </a>\n       (11,763),\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">\n        South Korea\n       </a>\n       (11,307), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">\n        Ukraine\n       </a>\n       (10,681). Though, predominantly white, Ohio has large black populations in all major metropolitan areas throughout the state, Ohio has a significant Hispanic population made up of Mexicans in Toledo and Columbus, and Puerto Ricans in Cleveland and Columbus, and also has a significant and diverse Asian population in Columbus.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The largest ancestry groups (which the Census defines as not including racial terms) in the state are:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        26.5%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">\n         German\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        14.1%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">\n         Irish\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        9.0%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">\n         English\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        6.4%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">\n         Italian\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        3.8%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">\n         Polish\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2.5%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_American" title="French American">\n         French\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.9%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_American" title="Scottish American">\n         Scottish\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.7%\n        <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Ohioans" title="Hungarian Ohioans">\n         Hungarian\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.6%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_American" title="Dutch American">\n         Dutch\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.5%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">\n         Mexican\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.2%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_American" title="Slovak American">\n         Slovak\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.1%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_American" title="Welsh American">\n         Welsh\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.1%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_American" title="Scotch-Irish American">\n         Scotch-Irish\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Ancestries claimed by less than 1% of the population include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_African" title="Sub-Saharan African">\n        Sub-Saharan African\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">\n        Puerto Rican\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_American" title="Swiss American">\n        Swiss\n American">\n        Romanian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_American" title="Austrian American">\n        Austrian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithuanian_American" title="Lithuanian American">\n        Lithuanian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finnish_American" title="Finnish American">\n        Finnish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indian_American" title="West Indian American">\n        West Indian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" title="Portuguese American">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovene_American" title="Slovene American">\n        Slovene\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_population_map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ohio_population_map.png/220px-Ohio_population_map.png" class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_population_map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ohio population density map.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">\n        Languages\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       About 6.7% of the population age 5 years and over reported speaking a language other than English, with 2.2% of the population speaking Spanish, 2.6% speaking other Indo-European languages, 1.1% speaking Asian and Austronesian languages, and 0.8% speaking other languages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_1-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Numerically: 10,100,586 spoke\n       <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">\n        English\n       </a>\n       , 239,229\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       , 55,970\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language_in_the_United_States" title="German language in the United States">\n        German\n       </a>\n       , 38,990\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_language_in_the_United_States" title="Chinese language in the United States">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       , 33,125\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       , and 32,019\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_in_the_United_States" title="French in the United States">\n        French\n       </a>\n       . In addition 59,881 spoke a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_language" title="Slavic language">\n        Slavic language\n       </a>\n       and 42,673 spoke another\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_languages" title="West Germanic languages">\n        West Germanic language\n       </a>\n       according to the 2010 Census.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio also had the nation\'s largest population of\n       <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">\n        Slovene speakers\n       </a>\n       , second largest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">\n        Slovak speakers\n       </a>\n       , second largest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_German_language" title="Pennsylvania German language">\n        Pennsylvania Dutch (German) speakers\n       </a>\n       , and the third largest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">\n        Serbian speakers\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">\n        Religion\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1036" data-file-width="702" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg/170px-Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg/255px-Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg/340px-Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Amish" title="Amish">\n          Amish\n         </a>\n         children on the way to school.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       According to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pew_Forum" title="Pew Forum">\n        Pew Forum\n       </a>\n       poll, as of 2008, 76% of Ohioans identified as Christian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEW_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PEW-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Specifically, 26% of Ohio\'s population identified as\n       <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">\n        Evangelical Protestant\n       </a>\n       , 22% as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainline_(Protestant)" title="Mainline (Protestant)">\n        Mainline Protestant\n       </a>\n       , and 21% as Catholic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEW_96-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PEW-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       17% of the population is unaffiliated with any religious body.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEW_96-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PEW-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       1.3% (148,380) were\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Ohio" title="History of the Jews in Ohio">\n        Jewish\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are also small minorities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">\n        Jehovah\'s Witnesses\n       </a>\n       (1%),\n       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">\n        Muslims\n       </a>\n       (1%),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">\n        Hindus\n       </a>\n       (&lt;0.5%),\n       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">\n        Buddhists\n       </a>\n       (&lt;0.5%),\n       <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">\n        Mormons\n       </a>\n       (&lt;0.5%), and other faiths (1-1.5%).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEW_96-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PEW-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">\n        Association of Religion Data Archives\n       </a>\n       (ARDA), in 2010 the largest denominations by adherents were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">\n        Catholic Church\n       </a>\n       with 1,992,567; the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">\n        United Methodist Church\n       </a>\n       with 496,232; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">\n        Evangelical Lutheran Church in America\n       </a>\n       with 223,253, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">\n        Southern Baptist Convention\n       </a>\n       with 171,000, the Christian Churches and Churches of Christ with 141,311, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Christ" title="United Church of Christ">\n        United Church of Christ\n       </a>\n       with 118,000, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">\n        Presbyterian Church (USA)\n       </a>\n       with 110,000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With about 70,000 people in 2015 Ohio had the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_Amish_population" title="List of U.S. states by Amish population">\n        largest Amish population of all states of the US\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the same data, a majority of Ohioans, 55%, feel that religion is "very important," 30% say that it is "somewhat important," and 15% responded that religion is "not too important/not important at all."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEW_96-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PEW-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       36% of Ohioans indicate that they attend religious services at least once weekly, 35% attend occasionally, and 27% seldom or never participate in religious services.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEW_96-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PEW-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ohio" title="Economy of Ohio">\n        Economy of Ohio\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Ohio locations by per capita income">\n        Ohio locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg/250px-Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg/375px-Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg/500px-Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cincinnati\'s Procter &amp; Gamble is one of Ohio\'s largest companies in terms of revenue.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2010, Ohio was ranked No. 2 in the country for best business climate by Site Selection magazine, based on a business-activity database.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state has also won three consecutive Governor\'s Cup awards from the magazine, based on business growth and developments.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2010\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Ohio\'s gross domestic product (GDP) was $478 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This ranks Ohio\'s economy as the seventh-largest of all fifty states and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia">\n        District of Columbia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Small Business &amp; Entrepreneurship Council ranked the state No. 10 for best business-friendly tax systems in their Business Tax Index 2009, including a top corporate tax and capital gains rate that were both ranked No. 6 at 1.9%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMEC_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SMEC-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio was ranked No. 11 by the council for best friendly-policy states according to their Small Business Survival Index 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Directorship\'s Boardroom Guide ranked the state No. 13 overall for best business climate, including No. 7 for best litigation climate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Forbes ranked the state No. 8 for best regulatory environment in 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio has 5 of the top 115 colleges in the nation, according to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report">\n        U.S. News and World Report\n       </a>\n       \'s 2010 rankings,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and was ranked No. 8 by the same magazine in 2008 for best high schools.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ohio\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" title="Unemployment rate">\n        unemployment rate\n       </a>\n       stands at 5.2% as of April 2015,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perkins_110-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-perkins-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       down from 10.7% in May 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state still lacks 45,000 jobs compared to the pre\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession_in_the_United_States" title="Great Recession in the United States">\n        recession\n       </a>\n       numbers of 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perkins_110-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-perkins-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The labor force participation as of April 2015 is 63%, slightly above the national average.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perkins_110-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-perkins-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio\'s per capita income stands at $34,874.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2007\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Ohio\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_household_income" title="Median household income">\n        median household income\n       </a>\n       is $46,645,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and 13.1% of the population is below the poverty line,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POVERTY_115-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-POVERTY-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       slightly above the national rate of 13%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POVERTY_115-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-POVERTY-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">\n        manufacturing\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_industry" title="Financial industry">\n        financial activities\n       </a>\n       sectors each compose 18.3% of Ohio\'s GDP, making them Ohio\'s largest industries by percentage of GDP.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio has the largest bioscience sector in the Midwest, and is a national leader in the "green" economy. Ohio is the largest producer in the country of plastics, rubber, fabricated metals, electrical equipment, and appliances.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       5,212,000 Ohioans are currently employed by wage or salary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By employment, Ohio\'s largest sector is trade/transportation/utilities, which employs 1,010,000 Ohioans, or 19.4% of Ohio\'s workforce, while the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_industry" title="Health care industry">\n        health care\n       </a>\n       and education sector employs 825,000 Ohioans (15.8%).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Government employs 787,000 Ohioans (15.1%), manufacturing employs 669,000 Ohioans (12.9%), and professional and technical services employs 638,000 Ohioans (12.2%).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio\'s manufacturing sector is the third-largest of all fifty United States states in terms of gross domestic product.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDOH_103-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DDOH-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Fifty-nine of the United States\' top 1,000 publicly traded companies (by revenue in 2008) are headquartered in Ohio, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">\n        Procter &amp; Gamble\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goodyear_Tire_%26_Rubber" title="Goodyear Tire &amp; Rubber">\n        Goodyear Tire &amp; Rubber\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AK_Steel" title="AK Steel">\n        AK Steel\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Timken_Company" title="Timken Company">\n        Timken\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Abercrombie_%26_Fitch" title="Abercrombie &amp; Fitch">\n        Abercrombie &amp; Fitch\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy\'s">\n        Wendy\'s\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CORPLIST_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CORPLIST-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ohio is also one of 41 states with its own lottery,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOTTO_118-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOTTO-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Lottery" title="Ohio Lottery">\n        Ohio Lottery\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOTTO2_119-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOTTO2-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Ohio Lottery has contributed over $15.5 billion to public education in its 34-year history.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOTTO3_120-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOTTO3-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_travel">\n        Ground travel\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Many major east-west transportation corridors go through Ohio. One of those pioneer routes, known in the early 20th century as "Main Market Route 3", was chosen in 1913 to become part of the historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Highway" title="Lincoln Highway">\n        Lincoln Highway\n       </a>\n       which was the first road across America, connecting New York City to San Francisco. In Ohio, the Lincoln Highway linked many towns and cities together, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">\n        Canton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Ohio" title="Mansfield, Ohio">\n        Mansfield\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Wooster,_Ohio" title="Wooster, Ohio">\n        Wooster\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lima,_Ohio" title="Lima, Ohio">\n        Lima\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Van_Wert,_Ohio" title="Van Wert, Ohio">\n        Van Wert\n       </a>\n       . The arrival of the Lincoln Highway to Ohio was a major influence on the development of the state. Upon the advent of the federal numbered highway system in 1926, the Lincoln Highway through Ohio became\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_30_(Ohio)" title="U.S. Route 30 (Ohio)">\n        U.S. Route 30\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ohio also is home to 228 miles (367\xc2\xa0km) of the Historic\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Road" title="National Road">\n        National Road\n       </a>\n       , now\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_40_in_Ohio" title="U.S. Route 40 in Ohio">\n        U.S. Route 40\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ohio has a highly developed network of roads and interstate highways. Major east-west through routes include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Turnpike" title="Ohio Turnpike">\n        Ohio Turnpike\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_80_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 80 (Ohio)">\n        I-80\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_90_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 90 (Ohio)">\n        I-90\n       </a>\n       ) in the north,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_76_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 76 (Ohio)">\n        I-76\n       </a>\n       through\n       <a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">\n        Akron\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_70_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 70 (Ohio)">\n        I-70\n       </a>\n       through\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">\n        Columbus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">\n        Dayton\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appalachian_Highway_(Ohio)" title="Appalachian Highway (Ohio)">\n        Appalachian Highway\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Route_32_(Ohio)" title="State Route 32 (Ohio)">\n        State Route 32\n       </a>\n       ) running from\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">\n        West Virginia\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">\n        Cincinnati\n       </a>\n       . Major north-south routes include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_75_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 75 (Ohio)">\n        I-75\n       </a>\n       in the west through\n       <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">\n        Toledo\n       </a>\n       , Dayton, and Cincinnati,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_71_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 71 (Ohio)">\n        I-71\n       </a>\n       through the middle of the state from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">\n        Cleveland\n       </a>\n       through Columbus and Cincinnati into\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_77_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 77 (Ohio)">\n        I-77\n       </a>\n       in the eastern part of the state from Cleveland through Akron,\n       <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">\n        Canton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Philadelphia,_Ohio" title="New Philadelphia, Ohio">\n        New Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Marietta,_Ohio" title="Marietta, Ohio">\n        Marietta\n       </a>\n       south into West Virginia. Interstate 75 between Cincinnati and Dayton is one of the heaviest traveled sections of interstate in Ohio.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ohio also has a highly developed network of signed state bicycle routes. Many of them follow\n       <a href="/wiki/Rail_trail" title="Rail trail">\n        rail trails\n       </a>\n       , with conversion ongoing. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_to_Erie_Trail" title="Ohio to Erie Trail">\n        Ohio to Erie Trail\n       </a>\n       (route 1) connects Cincinnati, Columbus, and Cleveland.\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bicycle_Route_50" title="U.S. Bicycle Route 50">\n        U.S. Bicycle Route 50\n       </a>\n       traverses Ohio from\n       <a href="/wiki/Steubenville,_Ohio" title="Steubenville, Ohio">\n        Steubenville\n       </a>\n       to the Indiana state line outside\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Indiana" title="Richmond, Indiana">\n        Richmond\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USRN_USBR_50_121-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USRN_USBR_50-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ohio has several long-distance hiking trails, the most prominent is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Buckeye_Trail" title="Buckeye Trail">\n        Buckeye Trail\n       </a>\n       which is a 1,444-mile (2,324\xc2\xa0km)[1] hiking trail that loops around the state of Ohio. Part of it is on roads and part is on wooded trail. Additionally, the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Country_Trail" title="North Country Trail">\n        North Country Trail\n       </a>\n       (the longest of the eleven\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Scenic_Trail" title="National Scenic Trail">\n        National Scenic Trails\n       </a>\n       authorized by\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">\n        Congress\n       </a>\n       ) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Discovery_Trail" title="American Discovery Trail">\n        American Discovery Trail\n       </a>\n       (a system of recreational trails and roads that collectively form a coast-to-coast route across the mid-tier of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       ) pass through Ohio. Much of these 2 trails coincide with the Buckeye Trail.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_travel">\n        Air travel\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Ohio" title="List of airports in Ohio">\n        List of airports in Ohio\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ohio has 5 international airports, 4 commercial and 2 military. The 5 international includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">\n        Cleveland Hopkins International Airport\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Glenn_Columbus_International_Airport" title="John Glenn Columbus International Airport">\n        John Glenn Columbus International Airport\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dayton_International_Airport" title="Dayton International Airport">\n        Dayton International Airport\n       </a>\n       , Ohio\'s third largest airport.\n       <a href="/wiki/Akron_Fulton_International_Airport" title="Akron Fulton International Airport">\n        Akron Fulton International Airport\n       </a>\n       handles cargo and for private use.\n       <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_International_Airport" title="Rickenbacker International Airport">\n        Rickenbacker International Airport\n       </a>\n       is one of two military airfields which is also home to the 7th largest FedEx building in America.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The other military airfield is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wright_Patterson_Air_Force_Base" title="Wright Patterson Air Force Base">\n        Wright Patterson Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       which is one of the largest Air Force bases in the United States. Other major airports are located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Toledo_Express_Airport" title="Toledo Express Airport">\n        Toledo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akron-Canton_Airport" title="Akron-Canton Airport">\n        Akron\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati/Northern_Kentucky_International_Airport" title="Cincinnati/Northern Kentucky International Airport">\n        Cincinnati/Northern Kentucky International Airport\n       </a>\n       is in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hebron,_Kentucky" title="Hebron, Kentucky">\n        Hebron, Kentucky\n       </a>\n       and therefore is not listed above.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_lists">\n        Transportation lists\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Ohio_state_highways" title="List of Ohio state highways">\n         List of Ohio state highways\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ohio_train_stations" title="List of Ohio train stations">\n         List of Ohio train stations\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ohio_railroads" title="List of Ohio railroads">\n         List of Ohio railroads\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Ohio_rivers" title="List of Ohio rivers">\n         List of Ohio rivers\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Historic_Ohio_Canals" title="Historic Ohio Canals">\n         Historic Ohio Canals\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">\n        Law and government\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ohio" title="Government of Ohio">\n        Government of Ohio\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2258" data-file-width="2812" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg/250px-Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg/375px-Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg/500px-Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Statehouse_columbus.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Capitol" title="Ohio State Capitol">\n          Ohio State Capitol\n         </a>\n         located in\n         <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">\n          Columbus, Ohio\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The state government of Ohio consists of the executive,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CO_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CO-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       judicial,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and legislative\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       branches.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">\n        Executive branch\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The executive branch is headed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Ohio" title="List of Governors of Ohio">\n        Governor of Ohio\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CO_122-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CO-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The current governor is\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Kasich" title="John Kasich">\n        John Kasich\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOV_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GOV-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican\n       </a>\n       elected in 2010. A\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Ohio" title="Lieutenant Governor of Ohio">\n        lieutenant governor\n       </a>\n       succeeds the governor in the event of any removal from office,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and performs any duties assigned by the governor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The current lieutenant governor is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_Taylor_(Ohio_politician)" title="Mary Taylor (Ohio politician)">\n        Mary Taylor\n       </a>\n       . The other elected constitutional offices in the executive branch are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Secretary_of_State" title="Ohio Secretary of State">\n        secretary of state\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Jon_A._Husted" title="Jon A. Husted">\n        Jon A. Husted\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Auditor" title="Ohio State Auditor">\n        auditor\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dave_Yost_(Ohio_politician)" title="Dave Yost (Ohio politician)">\n        Dave Yost\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Treasurer" title="Ohio State Treasurer">\n        treasurer\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josh_Mandel_(politician)" title="Josh Mandel (politician)">\n        Josh Mandel\n       </a>\n       ), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Attorney_General" title="Ohio Attorney General">\n        attorney general\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Mike_DeWine" title="Mike DeWine">\n        Mike DeWine\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CO_122-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CO-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">\n        Judicial branch\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       There are three levels of the Ohio state\n       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">\n        judiciary\n       </a>\n       . The lowest level is the court of common pleas: each county maintains its own constitutionally mandated court of common pleas, which maintain jurisdiction over "all justiciable matters".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-District_127-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-District-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The intermediate-level court system is the district court system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Twelve courts of appeals exist, each retaining jurisdiction over appeals from common pleas, municipal, and county courts in a set geographical area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-District_127-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-District-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A case heard in this system is decided by a three-judge panel, and each judge is elected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-District_127-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-District-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The highest-ranking court, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_Supreme_Court" title="Ohio Supreme Court">\n        Ohio Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       , is Ohio\'s "court of last resort".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCOO_129-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCOO-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A seven-justice panel composes the court, which, by its own\n       <a href="/wiki/Certiorari#State_courts" title="Certiorari">\n        discretion\n       </a>\n       , hears appeals from the courts of appeals, and retains original jurisdiction over limited matters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">\n        Legislative branch\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_General_Assembly" title="Ohio General Assembly">\n        Ohio General Assembly\n       </a>\n       is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">\n        bicameral\n       </a>\n       legislature consisting of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Senate" title="Ohio Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_House_of_Representatives" title="Ohio House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Senate is composed of 33 districts, each of which is represented by one senator. Each senator represents approximately 330,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">\n        constituents\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The House of Representatives is composed of 99 members.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_politics">\n        National politics\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ohio" title="Politics of Ohio">\n Grant">\n        Ulysses S. Grant\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">\n        Rutherford B. Hayes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">\n        James A. Garfield\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison" title="Benjamin Harrison">\n        Benjamin Harrison\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">\n        William McKinley\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">\n        William Howard Taft\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Harding" title="Warren G. Harding">\n        Warren G. Harding\n       </a>\n       ) to the\n       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">\n        White House\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HEINRICHS_135-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HEINRICHS-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All seven were\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Republican_Party" title="History of the United States Republican Party">\n        Republicans\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       native\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">\n        William Henry Harrison\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">\n        Whig\n       </a>\n       , resided in Ohio.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HEINRICHS_135-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HEINRICHS-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Historian R. Douglas Hurt asserts that not since Virginia "had a state made such a mark on national political affairs".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-holli162_136-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-holli162-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">\n         The Economist\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       notes that "This slice of the mid-west contains a bit of everything American\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 part north-eastern and part southern, part urban and part rural, part hardscrabble poverty and part booming suburb",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio is the only state that has voted for the winning Presidential candidate in each election since\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1964" title="United States presidential election, 1964">\n        1964\n       </a>\n       , and in 33 of the 37 held since the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        Civil War\n       </a>\n       . No Republican has ever won the presidency without winning Ohio.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Ohio\'s voter demographic leans towards the\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democratic Party\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISPATCH_138-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DISPATCH-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An estimated 2,408,178 Ohioans are registered to vote as Democrats, while 1,471,465 Ohioans are registered to vote as\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republicans\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISPATCH_138-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DISPATCH-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template">\n        <span style="white-space: nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">\n           <span title="\xc2\xa0Dead link since August 2012">\n            dead link\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       These are changes from 2004 of 72% and 32%, respectively, and Democrats have registered over 1,000,000 new Ohioans since 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISPATCH_138-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DISPATCH-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template">\n        <span style="white-space: nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">\n           <span title="\xc2\xa0Dead link since August 2012">\n            dead link\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_(voter)" title="Independent (voter)">\n        Unaffiliated voters\n       </a>\n       have an\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/attrition" title="wikt:attrition">\n        attrition\n       </a>\n       of 15% since 2004, losing an estimated 718,000 of their kind.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISPATCH_138-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DISPATCH-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template">\n        <span style="white-space: nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">\n           <span title="\xc2\xa0Dead link since August 2012">\n            dead link\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       The total now rests at 4,057,518 Ohioans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISPATCH_138-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DISPATCH-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template">\n        <span style="white-space: nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">\n           <span title="\xc2\xa0Dead link since August 2012">\n            dead link\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       In total, there are 7,937,161 Ohioans registered to vote.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISPATCH_138-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DISPATCH-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template">\n        <span style="white-space: nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">\n           <span title="\xc2\xa0Dead link since August 2012">\n            dead link\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Ohio,_2008" title="United States presidential election in Ohio, 2008">\n        United States presidential election of 2008\n       </a>\n       , then-\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">\n        Senator\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">\n        Illinois\n       </a>\n       won 51.50% of Ohio\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">\n        popular vote\n       </a>\n       , 4.59 percentage points more than his nearest rival, Senator\n       <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">\n        John McCain\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">\n        Arizona\n       </a>\n       (with 46.91% of the popular vote).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OSOS_139-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OSOS-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, Obama won only 22 of Ohio\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Ohio" title="List of counties in Ohio">\n        88 counties\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">\n        <a href="#cite_note-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since 2010, the Republicans have largely controlled Ohio state politics, including a super-majority in the state\'s House, a majority in the state Senate, the Governorship, etc.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elections.nytimes.com_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-elections.nytimes.com-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2014, the state Senate is 1 Republican away from a super-majority.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elections.nytimes.com_141-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-elections.nytimes.com-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Census,_2000" title="United States Census, 2000">\n        2000 census\n       </a>\n       , Ohio lost one\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_congressional_districts" title="List of United States congressional districts">\n        congressional district\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">\n        United States House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       , which leaves Ohio with 18 districts, and consequently, 18 representatives. The state lost two more seats following the 2010 Census, leaving it with 16 votes for the next 3 presidential elections in 2012, 2016 and 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_House_elections,_2008" title="United States House elections, 2008">\n        2008 elections\n       </a>\n       , Democrats gained three seats in Ohio\'s delegation to the House of Representatives.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This leaves eight Republican-controlled seats in the Ohio delegation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ohio\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">\n        U.S. Senators\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/112th_Congress" title="112th Congress">\n        112th Congress\n       </a>\n       are Republican\n       <a href="/wiki/Rob_Portman" title="Rob Portman">\n        Rob Portman\n       </a>\n       and Democrat\n       <a href="/wiki/Sherrod_Brown" title="Sherrod Brown">\n        Sherrod Brown\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcia_Kaptur" title="Marcia Kaptur">\n        Marcy Kaptur\n       </a>\n       (D-\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio%27s_9th_congressional_district" title="Ohio\'s 9th congressional district">\n        9\n       </a>\n       ) is the dean, or most senior member, of the Ohio delegation to the United States House of Representatives.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Ohio\'s system of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_education" title="Public education">\n        public education\n       </a>\n       is outlined in Article VI of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_Constitution" title="Ohio Constitution">\n        state constitution\n       </a>\n       , and in Title XXXIII of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Revised_Code" title="Ohio Revised Code">\n        Ohio Revised Code\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_University" title="Ohio University">\n        Ohio University\n       </a>\n       , the first university in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">\n        Northwest Territory\n       </a>\n       , was also the first public institution in Ohio. Substantively, Ohio\'s system is similar to those found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States" title="Education in the United States">\n        other states\n       </a>\n       . At the State level, the Ohio Department of Education, which is overseen by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Board_of_Education" title="Ohio State Board of Education">\n        Ohio State Board of Education\n       </a>\n       , governs primary and secondary educational institutions. At the municipal level, there are approximately 700 school districts statewide. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Board_of_Regents" title="Ohio Board of Regents">\n        Ohio Board of Regents\n       </a>\n       coordinates and assists with Ohio\'s institutions of higher education which have recently been reorganized into the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_System_of_Ohio" title="University System of Ohio">\n        University System of Ohio\n       </a>\n       under Governor Strickland. The system averages an annual enrollment of over 400,000 students, making it one of the five largest state university systems in the U.S.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_(Bachelor%27s_Degree).png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1126" data-file-width="2336" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_%28Bachelor%27s_Degree%29.png/440px-Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_%28Bachelor%27s_Degree%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_%28Bachelor%27s_Degree%29.png/660px-Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_%28Bachelor%27s_Degree%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_%28Bachelor%27s_Degree%29.png/880px-Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_%28Bachelor%27s_Degree%29.png 2x" width="440"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_Map_of_Majors_in_Ohio_(Bachelor%27s_Degree).png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A tree map depicting the distribution of bachelor\'s degrees awarded in Ohio in 2014.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span
